text:
These were fabulous! Everyone from Thanksgiving wanted the recipe. Followed exactly but next time I think I will cut the butter in half. Heres a hint to keep the potatoes from getting soggy in the crock. Lay a clean terry kitchen towel across the top of the crock then put the lid on. The towel absorbs the steam instead of it running back into the potatoes.

text:
Using sour cream and/or cream cheese in these mashed potatoes was nothing new to me. I've always used one or the other or both but I also always use either russet or Yukon Gold potatoes rather than red skinned. What intrigued me was the idea (duh) of making them ahead of time and then reheating them in the slow cooker. I used the terry towel suggestion, as well as the suggestion to stir them every now and then to prevent them from browning along the edges. As others did, I simply forgot to put the butter in at the last, but with the gravy, the butter wasn't even missed. This method of preparation really eased the busy-ness and hustle-bustle in the kitchen on Thanksgiving day. I'm hooked...I will always make the mashed potatoes this way on Thanksgiving from now on! Thanks for a simple solution to getting rid of at least one step of the Thanksgiving meal preparation. Thanks too, to those of you with the helpful suggestions!

text:
Very easy to prepare, and even easier to eat.  The flavors in this dish combined very well, and tasted like no other mashed potato dish I've ever had.  And it STAYED HOT throughout the whole meal, which is a rarity for any kind of mashed potato dish that I've ever fixed.  One slight problem was that the potatoes didn't mash thoroughly, which left smallish chunks of whole potato in, but even that wasn't enough to detract from the overall experience.  (If you're particular about it, I would suggest running a mixer through it before placing in your Crock.)  I was pinched for time, and set the Crock on HIGH for 1 hour - they still tasted just fine, so I'm not sure 3 hours on LOW is necessary.  (Tip:  halve the time if you're cooking on HIGH - 3 hours on LOW equals 1 1/2 hours on HIGH, just a helpful thing to know when cooking with Crock-Pots.)  Excellent dish.  Thanks, Bwaye, this will be going into my regular rotation!

text:
Very nice recipe! I make this recipe with light sour cream and light cream cheese. My husband tasted the potatoes before I added any butter and he said they were great as they were and since we were going to be serving them with gravy adding butter would make it too rich. I'll be making this again next week for Thanksgiving; I know it'll be a hit and best of all I won't have to be rushing around getting the potatoes ready while company is over. Thanks!
UPDATE (11/09):I have made this for each Thanksgiving since I first tried them, and they have always gotten many complements. For those that have wondered how much this makes volume-wise, one and a half recipes (so, 12 servings worth) fills up my 6 qt slow cooker. We serve it for 16 people at Thanksgiving and generally have some left over since there are so many other dishes on the table. I have used both red and russet potatoes and always leave the skin on, and it is very good both ways. Thanks again for a great, no-fail recipe!

text:
I've been making these every holiday for several years and I'm always asked to bring the potatoes now, so they are obviously a hit! Like others, I most often use Yukon Gold, but red potatoes work well too. I increase the garlic to 3 Tbsp and I base the number of chicken bouillon cubes on how much water I boil the potatoes in. It's usually 9 cups or so, thus I use 9 cubes. It makes for a great flavor as the potatoes cook in the liquid. Also like others, I've forgotten to top off with butter and it is not missed at all except for the added calories!  This is a great way to free up my stove and oven and have one less thing to worry about during Thanksgiving or Christmas because I make these the night before, take out of the fridge about an hour before I turn on the slow cooker and they are hot and delicious (with occassional stirring!), in a few hours.

text:
This is an awesome recipe for make-ahead mashed potatoes! I think that some of the cooks who gave this low reviews miss the point - this recipe and preparation aren't supposed to save you time. You do still have to peel, boil, mash, etc.... The point is: You don't have the last minute rush trying to make the mashed potatoes just when everything else is ready. You don't have to worry that your potatoes are ready too early when other things are still cooking, and might get cold before you put them on the table. You don't have to worry that you put your potatoes on a burner "just to keep them warm" and they end up scorching by accident. You can make these and take to a friend's or a potluck, and no matter what else is cooking, all you need is a little bit of counter space and a plug in. Plus, these are just really super tasty. I love my own traditional butter and milk mashed potatoes too, but this recipe is a close second... maybe tied since it is so nice to be able to make them ahead of time.  I took the suggestions to use a cloth towel in between crock and lid while cooking (also used when the crock was in the fridge overnight, before cooking). When I was mashing everything I was a bit worried because it was very runny... it didn't stay that way. I didn't add butter after cooking, because I thought they were rich enough, and didn't want to make them runny again.   Everyone loved them, and I will definitely make again.

I usually make half of this recipe which gives us six modest servings.  I usually freeze my leftovers and have them ready and waiting in the freezer for busy nights. text:
Delicious! Made these to accompany tonight's roast chicken dinner. My hubs thought these were the BOMB and the best taters I've ever made! Although I don't completely agree (I'm still a sucker for plain 'ol mashed potatoes), I must admit, these are prolly the best "fancied up" potatoes I've had in a long while. I'll for sure serve BWAYE's potatoes when I want a special, make-ahead treat! NOTE: Feel free to use reduced-fat or fat-free dairy products. I used reduced-fat sour cream / ff cream cheese and STILL felt indulgent. :) NOTE #2: The towel trick really works (it prevents the water that condenses on your sc lid from dripping down into your potatoes, making them soggy). Stirring every now and then also helps prevent browning on the sides (if appearance matters to you - it doesn't affect the flavor in the least). Thanksgiving dinner will be EVEN better this year now that I found this recipe. :-) Thanks for sharing, BWAYE!

text:
The dish itself was okay. Definitely nothing to write home about but it was all the work I had to do that makes me not want to give this more than 2 stars. When I saw the good rating, I had high hopes. I personally thought it was just like the box stuff. Didn't see any huge difference. And the fact that you have to cook the potatoes and mash them with other ingredients BEFORE putting in the slow cooker doesn't make any sense. Before I tried this recipe, I said to myself "Wait a minute, it looks like mashed potatoes are done in step #1.Then why put it in the slow cooker when it's already done? And then I thought MAYBE putting it in the slow cooker would actually make some difference in the flavor or something so I decided to give it a try. Nope, there's no difference at all in the flavor. I think I actually liked the flavor of "before slow cooker" better. It just doesn't make any sense that you make mashed potatoes and then put that done dish in slow cooker for more time. Why? It's just so redundant. Now I have one more big dish to wash and thinking of all the work and time I wasted to make mediocre mashed potatoes just upsets me so much.

This was so good.  I love boiling the potatoes in bouillon and garlic- it adds such flavor!  I used boullion powder and just pressed two cloves of garlic, leaving them in large chunks so I could mash them up with the potatoes.  I used light sour cream, next time I will try light cream cheese too.  (Although it tasted wonderful, it was kind of heavy.)  I only had one red potato left, so I used that along with a bunch of Yukon Golds.    I cut the recipe in half and only added 2 TB of butter at the end, and it probably didn't even need any butter- it was so rich already!  I only added a few spoonfuls of the reserved water also.  Served this with Roast Sticky Chicken from this site.  I think I will make these for Thanksgiving this year!

I used Yukon Golds instead of red potatoes, chicken broth instead of the bouillon & water, and added cheddar and green onions to make them like twice-baked potatoes.  I really like the idea of boiling the potatoes in chicken broth and fresh minced garlic...it gave the potatoes an unbelievable flavor!!  I didn't add any additional moisture to the mashed potatoes, but I think next time I might add some milk at the very end with the butter (I actually forgot to add the butter...they weren't bad but I will remember to put it in next time!!).  On a normal day, I would agree with most of the reviews saying that the crock pot is probably unnecessary...but on Thanksgiving, you need all the extra help you can get and these work out perfectly for the big day.

text:
Honestly, for all the calories that are in it, I was disappointed.  Maybe because I did forget a few things...I forgot to add the garlic and also left out the chicken bouillon to accommodate my vegetarian guests. I also didn't add the full recommendation for butter at the end because I ran out, so maybe I added 2 Tbsp in stead of 1/2 cup.  

So, just with the sour cream and cream cheese and a little bit of salt & pepper, it left it tasting rich but bland (is that possible?!)

I like the idea of using the crockpot to save time, but really, what's the real point, if you're doing everything you normally would to mashed potatoes (adding the extras and mashing everything up) after boiling the potatoes and just sticking it in the crockpot to keep it warm? It takes the same amount of time...

In the future I'll just stick to my usual milk/salt/ and lots of butter routine. Maybe I'll try the chicken bouillon next time, it does sound yummy, but I'll leave out the cream cheese.

This is an EXCELLENT recipe for mashed potatoes!  I wouldn't change it up except to add the butter, salt and pepper the last 30 minutes of slow-cooking time. Well done!

text:
I make this so much easier and much better flavor by putting all my ingredients at one time in the slow cooker, except NO water!  I layer my cream, butter, potatoes, 3 triangles of spreadable cheese,  4 oz. cream cheese, salt & pepper, garlic (if you like), then repeat layers. If I need more liquid, I add heavy cream mixed with chicken or vege broth. I only have to check on and stir 2 -3 times while cooking on low either overnight or during the day. You will get the richest real potato flavor because you are not pouring off the potato starches. And those brown edges around the edge, stir them into the potatoes. Adds yummy richness. You will truly taste a huge difference in the potato flavor! I have recommended this recipe to so many of my family and friends and they absolutely love it. In a hurry? Use your pressure cooker!   Enjoy!

text:
Use this recipe every Thanksgiving.  We have at least 14 people every year, so I try to make as much as I can.  I usually can fit about 8-9 lbs of potatoes in my crockpot.  I usually add a little more cream cheese and sour cream b/c of the extra potatoes and extra garlic in the boiling water and chicken broth.  I have a wheat allergy so i find it easier to use chicken broth without wheat starch or msg and just add a large can or box of broth to the water.  I use my hand mixer as I found out my stand mixer is too small for all those potatoes.  I have found two hours is perfect so you don't get the brown edges and like the suggestion of just stirring once in awhile.  I also have noted that the potatoes thin a little when cooking but didn't have a problem with that this year, but the towel idea is a good one too. Our favorite part about these potatoes is they stay warm the whole meal.  love it!

The ultimate in convenience coupled with taste--this recipe's a keeper!  Hint: Since you're using the slow cooker anyway, cut up the taters and put them into the slow cooker, add the broth, and let them cook themselves.  When they're tender, proceed with the rest of the recipe.  I made this to feed 32 people (no, it didn't all fit in one slow cooker)--good stuff.  I also left out the butter, as the taters were really rich.  I froze the leftovers and, re-cooked, they still taste great.

text:
Oh wow!  This recipe is absolutely delicious!!!  I will not go back to fixing mashed potatoes like I did years ago!  I think cooking the potatoes in the chicken bouillon water is the secret!  This mashed potato dish last several days and can be reheated after the first serving. I peel the potatoes,cut into chunk size (for cooking) and keep the potatoes covered under water in a big bowl. I then placed the bowl in the refrigerator (to keep from browning) the night before making this dish to cut down on preparation time.  Drain the refrigerated water off the potatoes when ready to cook and then prepare recipe in a crock pot as instructed.   Stir occasionally!  This recipe is so easy as a crock pot side dish. Especially easy for Thanksgiving meal.

text:
Delicious for our Thanksgiving meal and so nice to make ahead!  

I used 10 pounds of Russet Potatoes.  Followed the recipe part of the way, however, I cut out lots of unwanted fat grams.  The garlic and broth makes a wonderful flavor.  I did use one can of reduced soduim chicken broth instead of the 3 cubes.  

(When potatoes are ready for draining... SAVE the water flavor for your gravy.  It really adds a nice taste.)  

I beat the potatoes with only 2 cups of reduced sour cream and flavored with salt and pepper.  

Refrigerated overnight, the next day I warmed them slightly in the microwave, and placed in a crock pot on low stirring them once in a while.  

Using a terry cloth towel between potatoes and lid does help keep the water drippings off the potatoes when lifting up the lid as someone else suggested.  

Add your gravy to the potatoes and you have one awesome tasting side dish!!!  This recipe is a keeper.

text:
The concept of having a side dish in the crockpot is a good idea for family holiday meals so I decided to try this recipe.  It will be good for future holiday meals with a few tweaks.  I think you have to remember that for a crockpot or slow cooker to work well, it needs to be 1/2 to 2/3 full.  Less than that and it overcooks, and more than that it won't get hot enough.  Well, I had too much in my crockpot so it didn't get hot enough and the center was really cold.  I didn't realize this until it was close to meal time.  Next time I will only fill the pot to 2/3 full.  Also, when I started the turkey that I served with this, I put a foil pack containing a whole bulb of garlic drizzled with olive oil.  I cooked this until soft and added it to the potatoes instead of the minced garlic.  Either works, I just prefer the flavor of the roasted garlic.

text:
I made these for a work Thanksgiving gathering and since I work at 8am and the luncheon wasn't held until 12pm, this recipe could not have been more convenient! I refrigerated the potatoes overnight, then placed them in a slow cooker on my desk until lunch...they were absolutely awesome and I'm glad I was one of the first in line, because rumor has it that these had completely disappeared before the 10th person in line made it up!! I did use the garlic cream cheese, so I omitted the garlic when cooking. Also, I did NOT place a terry cloth over the slow cooker, as I personally didn't mind a little extra moisture - I figured it may even keep the potatoes from drying out. I will be making these again for Christmas dinner on Friday night, and I think rather than salt that I will add a pinch of garlic salt for a little extra flavor, as well as green onion, which I think will go excellent with these. Thanks BWAYE for a great recipe!

text:
This was really good but there were some problems.  I followed the recipe pretty closely except I added a couple of teaspoons of oregano.  As for the problems, first, the garlic taste is very weak.  If you like the taste of garlic, you'll need to add some raw garlic to the final product.  Also, I made the potatoes the day before serving and they were absolutely delicious right after being mixed with the cream cheese and sour cream (I creamed the cream cheese and sour cream together first to help everything blend easily).  But, the next day, for some reason, after heating them up in the crock pot, they just didn't taste as well.  I added a little milk cuz they were real solid, mixed in the butter which was way too much, added some raw garlic and more oregano and they were just okay.  The really weird thing is, a few days later we heated the leftovers up in the crock pot and once again they were absolutely delicious albeit sinfully fattening.  I don't think I would make these again.....I think I could make equally delicious mashed potatoes without so many rich and fattening ingredients.  BTW, I made chicken noodle soup with the liquid the potatoes cooked in and it came out fantastic!

text:
These were the BEST mashed potatoes I have ever had. 

I wanted to have a somewhat healthier version, so I did not add any salt (plenty in the boullion). I also used half of the cream cheese and half the butter, but all the sour cream. Since I was "taking out" some of the flavor by cutting these out/down, I decided to add garlic.  I roasted one head of garlic while boiling the potatoes and then added it into the crockpot for the entire cooking time.  

The garlic added lots of flavor, but wasn't super garlicy.  I could have easily added another entire head of garlic for a real garlic flavor.

text:
Very good potatoes and none left over this year.  I used chicken broth in place of the boullion and added it back in slowly so not to make the potatoes soupy.  Also added the cream cheese and sour cream in small amounts.  Ended up using almost 16 ounces of sour cream and 2 boxes of cream cheese.  I probably used about 8 pounds of new potatoes with the skins left on. My slow cooker cooks really hot so I did not leave them in much more than 1 hour on low and then switched it to keep warm.  I added some butter and about 4 pieces of crispy bacon before serving.  Some chives or green onions would be good also.  I did place the terry cloth towel between the crock pot and the lid and did not have soupy potatoes at all but then they were not soupy to begin with.

text:
This recipe is wonderful and my 14 yr old just said, "it gets better with each taste." I don't know what to compare it to, but I love that it can go in the slow cooker...and the flavors were all enhanced during the time it was in the slow cooker. A couple of comments - I hate not knowing exactly how much liquid to add - I wanted at least a ball park idea (I used 1 1/4 cups...was that enough?...I was afraid to use too much). I used a potato masher, but it still left small chunks of potatoes and wasn't totally smooth. I happened to love that, but it was off putting to my 11 yr old daughter. Overall, I feel like it was missing something, but not sure what...next time I will definitely add more garlic. Also, it takes much much longer than 15 minutes to prepare 5 lbs of potatoes!! You have to wash, cut (and peel if you have picky eaters), then boil water and THEN cook them for 15 minutes, and finally mash and add all the extras. All of that takes closer to 45 minutes...but I'm a novice mashed potato maker. I accidentally added the butter before the slow cooker and it was fine. Next time I will put the potatoes in the mixer to get a smoother texture.

text:
I used yellow yukon potatoes peeled, and omitted the chicken bouillon because I like to keep recipes as low salt as possible.  I just know that people will be salting their food at the table, regardless of whether or not it was salted during cooking.  I also added fresh, chopped chives. I've made a similar recipe many times as I like to get the potatoes out of the way the day before.  They keep very well in the fridge, as long as they are covered!  This works best if they are allowed to come back to room temperature before cooking in the crock pot.  Also, one trick for fluffier mashed potatoes is to mash with a ricer or a masher rather than a mixer.

text:
These potatoes are awesome!  I followed the recipe except that I used russet potatoes and 4 cloves of garlic (boiled in the water with the potatoes).  I also used a mixer to whip in the rest of the ingredients before putting them into the slow cooker.  I was a little leery about adding so much sour cream and cream cheese, so I added it a little at a time.  I ended up putting all in that the recipe called for.  All they do is enhance the dish, they do not overpower the potatoes at all.  This is also a wonderful recipe to take to holiday potlucks because it stays warm.  Oh, and I also followed another reviewers suggestion to put a dish towel in the top to absorb the moisture and it worked wonderfully.

text:
This is a good mashed potato; a little different, but good. I added a little extra garlic to the finished product. For the fact that the crock pot is just an extra pot to clean please remember this. This recipe serves two purposes: 1) To produce a good mashed potato and 2) To allow you to prepare ahead of time and keep them warm until serving. You can certainly make these and serve them immediately. They are just as good. But those of you who want to get them done ahead of time has this option with the crock pot. I personally like the fact that I can make these beforehand, keep them warm and not be mashing potatoes at the last minute. So for me it is worth the extra couple minutes to clean the pot. Either method is fine and both produce a good end product.

text:
Delicious! And oh so easy to prepare.  The only change I made was to use yukon gold potatoes and add 2-3 Tbsp. of freeze dried chives.  This recipe will definitely go in the recipe box to make again.  Rather than throw away the reserved cooking water I saved it but wasn't really sure what I was going to do with it.  That is until now.  I brought the reserved cooking water up to a simmer then added some instant mashed potato flakes (I used about 1/2 pouch (from a 2 pouch box) of Publix brand roasted garlic), wisked until smooth then wisked in a little cheddar cheese.  And now I have some fairly decent, easy to make potato soup.

text:
I have made this recipe many times (as is as well as with minor alterations) and the results are always delicious! In fact, the mashed potatoes are so good people ask for the recipe and always want to take some home with them to devour (if the slow cooker is not empty). Here are some of the alterations I have made and why: (1) Scrubbed potatoes and leave skin on -- just because I am lazy sometimes and don't feel like peeling potatoes; (2) Vegetable bouillon cubes -- for those with a poultry allergy; (3) no bouillon and just boiled potatoes in plain water with the the garlic -- for those with an onion allergy. I just add more salt when using water. Not using bouillon is probably healthier anyway. (4) Keep a jar of reserved potato water near the slow cooker in case we need to add more if the potatoes seem to be getting a little dry.

text:
Super tasty!  Received lots of compliments on Thanksgiving.  And even better - you can make them ahead of time.  I made them the day before exactly as recipe stated - then placed in the slow cooker removable bowl and refrigerated them over night.  The morning of Thanksgiving I put the bowl in the slow cooker and turned them on low.  Be sure to reserve the water they were boiled in - I mixed this in small amounts until the consistency loosened up to where I wanted them.  Keep stirring every so often.  They were hot and very flavorful come meal time.  Definitely my mashed potato keeper recipe for Thanksgiving!!!

text:
Amazing!! I have made this recipe 4 times in the past 6 weeks and each time they have been the highlight of the meal! I will never make mashed potatoes any other way. The first time I made the recipe exactly as outlined, but have now perfected the recipe to my liking. I use yellow potatoes, and cut the sour cream in half, added a little more butter, garlic salt and parsley flakes. Talk about melt in your mouth, no need for gravy deliciousness! I found that boiling the potatoes a little longer helps with the creamy texture I like. If you like your potatoes lumpy, boil as directed. I placed paper towels between the lid and potatoes, I recommend this. I have made this the day before and placed the crockpot in the fridge overnight and cooked in the crockpot the next day and also made them with 3 hours til meal time, both were wonderful! Everyone will want your recipe. Enjoy!

text:
I made these this morning for Thanksgiving. I am going to follow other suggestions I took them out of fridge at 11am and let them sit for an hour to warm up and then covered the crock with a clean kitchen towel and cooked for 3 hours. I added a little more of the reserved liquid and stirred them a few times while they were cooking in crock pot.  I doubled this recipe using 10 pounds of red potatoes, and this filled up my large crock pot (I'm cooking for 30).  I decided to add 3 pounds of cooked crumbled bacon and have already added some salt and white pepper, they  taste amazing. I reserved a lot of the cooking liquid and I used about two cups when first mashing the potatoes.  This is the easiest way I have found to make mashed potatoes for a huge crowd.

text:
I adjusted the recipe for 8 lbs. of potatoes and it filled my large slow cooker very nicely.  I added much more garlic and a few tablespoons of Montreal Steak Seasoning.  I also added heavy cream ( a luxury because these potatoes were for a wedding celebration) until nice & creamy.  I cooked on high for about an hour and then switched to low for about three more hours. I did use the towel on top underneath the lid and it really makes a difference in capturing the moisture.  I also stirred the potatoes about once each hour and added about a cup of shredded cheddar cheese towards the end.  I forgot to add the butter but it was not missed.  The potatoes were excellent and were gone quickly at the party.  So easy but so delicious.

When I first read the ingredients list I wasn't sure about the cream cheese and the slow cooker method. text:
I needed a large amount of mashed potatoes for a 12-16 dinner party, that was not at my home.  So I was looking for a way to keep the potatoes warm, that would not be an inconvenience to the host (knowing that their kitchen is small and would be filled with many dishes needing warming).

Using a slow cooker is the perfect way to serve large amounts of mashed potatoes!  I have not used cream cheese before, with my mashed potatoes and found that it blends well with the sour cream.  I used fat free for both the cream cheese and sour cream, the flavor and texture were both great.  I did end up using butter and added it before hand.  Next time, I will try without...to save on the calories.

For the potatoes, I used 2 - 5 pound bags of red potatoes (peeled).

text:
Definitely the best mashed potatoes.  The first time I made these was 2 years ago for a Thanksgiving dinner at the office.  I have never in my life heard people rave so much about potatoes!  That's all they talked about for days.  It blew my mind the *mashed potatoes* were the highlight of the entire Thanksgiving dinner!  Even months later, my coworkers were emailing me telling me they had made these for dinner the night before.   I personally don't find them to be a lot of work.  I tend to peel my potatoes, so that's the hardest part -- everything else is compeltely easy.  The red potatoes are the key, though.  I made these with russet potatoes this weekend because I had gotten a great deal, and the flavors don't develop as well with the russets.  I was cooking for a vegetarian so I had also substituted vegetable stock for the chicken bouillon.  Don't get me wrong, they were still better than any other mashed potatoes I've eaten, just not quite as good as they are with the baby reds.   Anyway, YUM, they're delicious.  My boyfriend, coworkers, and family beg for these potatoes, and I don't blame them at all.

This is a good recipe. I left the red skins on, mostly because I'm lazy but it ended up looking and tasting great this way. Used the towel trick to cut down on moisture. I drained all but maybe 1/4 cup of the water and that was plenty, I didn't need to add any more water/milk. Also, I didn't want to boil the garlic with the potatoes because I didn't want to lose any in draining (garlic lover), so I tossed the garlic in some olive oil, wrapped in tinfoil and threw in my toaster oven for like 10 min at 250 f. Then I chopped it up and threw it in after everything else was mashed together. Got lots of compliments at Thanksgiving. Will make again!

I've been using this recipe for almost two years now and am just now getting around to rating it.  It's awesome, but I skip the slow cooker altogether (I usually am using it for roast beef or something to go with it, i'm a slow cooker junkie)  I did notice that the potatoes thinned out when I used to slow  cooker, but I like mine chunky and smashed instead of whipped and creamy, so now, to cut back on time wasted I just boil the potatoes (sometimes in just water if I dont have buillon and dont feel like chopping up garlic), smash them with cream cheese (try the herb and chive for flavor) and sour cream.  I also use less since I dont want to be a lard booty.

text:
These are more like keep warm potatoes than they are slow cooked. I give this recipe 4 stars because of what they add makes them perfect. They would get 5 stars if they recommended cooking them in the crockpot from the get go.
Just toss cubed potatoes, 1 stick of butter cubed, 1 tablespoon of chicken Better Than Bouillon (or 3 cubes), 2 teaspoons minced garlic, and 1/2 teaspoon pepper together in a 6-quart slow cooker. Add 1 cup of water, then cover, and cook on high until the potatoes are tender, about 3-4 hours. (The potatoes might have browned lightly in spots but that is okay.) Drain some of the liquid if there is still a lot. Mash with sour cream and milk, then enjoy.

Love these! I got so many compliments when I made these, they've become a staple for holidays.  I typically use a few cloves of roasted garlic but that's the only change. I would suggest reducing the sour cream a bit (it can be a tad sour with that if you're not careful). The first time I made these I didn't have an issue with burning but the second time they burned after about 4 hours. I suggest after 2 hours, stir them every 45 minutes or so and keep them on low or warm.

text:
Yes!!!!! Thank you so much for this recipe. I made these for two holiday pot-lucks, and people loved them. Im not sure how necessary it is to use a slow cooker, they would probably be amazing just right away like regular mashed potatoes. However, I love the addition of the slow cooker because it allows me to start cooking them early and gives me plenty of time to get ready for whatever event Im making them for, so I dont have to worry about them. I did what others mentioned with putting a towel on top of the cooker to prevent excess condensation from running into the potatoes.. works great! The recipe itself is SO simple. I hate peeling potatoes.. so I love that this calls for red potatoes, so much easier. You really dont need to put much of the reserved cooking liquid in before mashing, especially since the butter you eventually add melts and adds more liquid as well. I did need to add a fair amount of salt to these at the end, and Im not really someone that cooks with a lot of salt. They were just a little bland. I will also say that I think saying this serves 8 is only true if you are feeding 8 lumberjacks! I brought them to a party with 15 people, and I came home with a plastic container full of leftovers, not that Im complaining. :-)

country:

text:
These were surprisingly bland,  even though I used the chives & onion flavored cream cheese --- a full 8 ounce container, as the recipe states, and the full 8 oz container of sour cream.  I added 1 teaspoon salt and 1/2 teaspoon black pepper as I was mashing, and it was still bland. I then added 1/2 t garlic powder, which made it better, but the consistency was also kind of glue-like and heavy/thick. 

I know how to make good mashed potatoes, so it is not user error.  This is just a heavier, thicker recipe. Some people may like it, which explains the good reviews, but it just isn't anything special and is less good, texture-wise, than just using butter & milk. 

I was planning to use this for our Christmas Eve dinner, am so glad I did a trial run first, because now I know I will not make these.  It's a bit annoying to have wasted the ingredients and the money,  as I ended up throwing away almost all of this, but it is better than stressing on Christmas Eve and have a dish that just isn't very good. I always recommend a trial run.

If you do make these, a few this: 1) Absolutely use a terry dish towel under the crockpot lid, and stir every 30 mns or so. 2)  Cook on Low for 3 hours. 3) Do use the butter at the end to help with the texture and flavor, but start with half a stick (4 oz) instead of the whole thing, and go from there. 5) Leave the skin of the red potatoes on. It's pretty and tastes nice, and makes much less prep work.

text:
These are absolutely amazing!! My family loves them. I feel the real key to making these good is the chicken bouillon. It gives such a full flavor to the potatoes. I've even had to skip the cream cheese or sour cream at times (just didn't have them on hand) and as long as I have the bouillon they turn out great! By the way, if you ever HAVE to make instant potatoes, try throwing bouillon in the water and you'll be amazed at what a difference it will make. I tried it when I had to make potatoes for a crowd right before surgery and people thought they were real.

text:
I've made this recipe for years now. I love it and so does everyone else. Here are my tips for this recipe after making it about 30 times.. . 1. Add half of the given amounts of cream cheese and sour cream, taste the potatoes, and add more carefully to taste. Sometimes I love having the full amounts but my husband does not. 2. When adding your reserved water back into your potatoes, do so carefully or you'll add too much and make mushy potatoes, and always scoop up from the bottom of the bowl where you'll find the garlic hiding. If you really want to be an over achiever, use something to strain your water and put all of the garlic and seasonings into your potatoes. I use my sifter because it has tiny screen holes but I bet there's an easier way to do it.  3. For heavenly loaded mashed potatoes add shredded cheese, bacon bits, and green onions. 4. If you do add too much water, just cook up a bit of plain instant mashed potatoes and add them in for a quick rescue. 5. Skip the crock pot unless you need to transport the potatoes or keep them warmed.

I am on mashed potato duty for Easter, Thanksgiving and Christmas when our entire large family gets together. I like to use this recipe with the exception of using reduced sodium chicken broth instead of bullion cubes and water for my dad's dietary needs  and no garlic just for our personal taste. The convince of making these ahead to avoid the rush is the key here. I too, use the kitchen towel and crock pot liner. I will be traveling to my son and daughter-in-laws out of state this year for the first time since their marriage and I'll be taking this recipe with me. I'll also pass this on to my mom who will be making the Thanksgiving potatoes. Our Thanksgiving dressing will also be made on the counter in a second crock pot, using it for the entire cooking time.

text:
TASTY!  These are the new hit at our house - made them Christmas Day and heard only positive remarks (and the empty slow cooker spoke to how much our group liked them).
I made the recipe with one *slight* alteration - I used Herb & Garlic cream cheese - because I wanted them to have a bit of punch.  Everything else I did exactly as stated.  The cooking time was perfect and the potatoes (with skins on) were easy to mash.  
I used someone's earlier suggestion of having a clean terry cloth dishtowel under the lid to collect moisture and to avoid the potatoes from becoming watery - worked like a charm!  I stirred every hour or so and in total mine were in the slow cooker about 5 hours.  
This served 10 people (with many taking seconds) and nothing was left. 
Will make again!

These are very tasty mashed potatoes.  Made them last year for Christmas dinner (everyone loved them), and realized when I went looking for the recipe for this years dinner that I had never rated the recipe. 
Took a few tips from others and put a linen dish towel under lid to absorb condensation, stirred occasionally while in the crock and to save a few calories omitted butter at the end and never missed it.  
Saves a burner on the stove and also eliminates the last minute mashing of the potatoes.

text:
I agree with this rating, but only assigned 4 stars, because despite following the tip to use the towel under the lid to keep the condensation from dripping on to the potatoes, after they had sad for a while, they were too soft for my liking.  I also think the instructions should mention that using a hand mixer will help create the smooth fluffy texture most prefer.  I would add less of the boullion cooking water at the beginning, leaving the potatoes thicker than I want them to be at serving time.  Once the sour cream and cream cheese melt, the consistency changes.  We left out the garlic, but everyone REALLY liked them, and it was a huge advantage to make them in advance, keep them warm, and free up the stove using the slow cooker.  Superb flavour, and the boullion cooking water into the gravy was also a great addition.  Thanks for sharing...everyone wants the recipe.

I would recommend putting them on longer in the slow cooker in the morning at the low temp. I cranked it up to high for the last hour and they were warm, but not toasty war. I had no problem with moisture either. The taste was amazing! Definitely make these again.

text:
I was a little intimidated by the amount of fat the original recipe calls for, so I used the suggestions of others and bought fat-free sour cream and neufchatel cream cheese (33% less fat & softer than regular cream cheese).  Before mixing them into the potatoes I tried the fat-free sour cream and it is TERRIBLE.  It was time to cook so I quickly substituted Greek yogurt.  Instead of adding a lot of butter at the end, I added three big pats to the top of the potatoes when they were nearly done. Instead of minced garlic, I roasted a bulb and mashed it into the mix.  
They were great!  My husband, who has never had yogurt and never will, and probably can't even spell it, also thought they were great.  I've never seen him not add butter to mashed potatoes before pouring on the gravy (one reason I only make mashed potatoes on Thanksgiving), but he didn't add butter to these and didn't miss it.  This recipe's a keeper!

I have been using an almost identical recipe that cooks in the oven instead of the slow cooker.  I'm never going back!   The slow cooker kept the potatoes creamy and hot.  It also freed up the oven for other things.  I made the potatoes a day in advance and just stored them in my slow cooker liner in the frig ( no extra container to clean and no time adjustment).  They were perfect.  I did use low fat cream cheese and sour cream.  Following other's advice I left out the butter and it wasn't missed.  My company and family loved them!

Wonderful mashed potatoes, and even more wonderful was making them the day before Thanksgiving! I chose Yukon Gold potatoes and used a ricer for my mashed potatoes, for a nice creamy texture without any gumminess. I saved a jar of the potato water just in case...I refrigerated the potatoes overnight and put them in the crock pot on low for an hour, then switched to warm for 2 more hours, stirring 2 or 3 times. Perfect, I didn't need to add any of the potato water, and I used the whole stick of butter. Everyone loved these potatoes, thanks!

This was incredibly easy!  I used Yukon Gold Potatoes (5 lbs), which I peeled and quartered ahead of time - put them in cold water and stored in the fridge until ready to boil. text:
This was a great dish, but I feel it needed some gravy or additional garlic butter to make it GREAT...  

This is what I did:
- Cubed red potatoes the night before to cut down on Thanksgiving-day prep time
- Boiled potatoes with salt and lots of garlic
- Mashed potatoes with low-fat sour cream, garlic & herb cream cheese, veggie stock, and white wine
- Cooked on low for 3 hours

Potatoes were hot and creamy, but lacked something...this is why I recommend either a light turkey gravy or some serious garlic butter to complete the dish.  ENJOY!
